# Project ID: 3cbc2725-bc6e-4979-9476-92e1f163b5c9 - Title: Cyber Security For Employees
**PROJECT INFORMATION**

*   **Project Name:** Cyber Security For Employees
*   **Business Unit:** IT
*   **Target Audience:** All Employees
*   **Experience Level:** 0-2 years
*   **Date:** 2026-02-21

**COURSE OVERVIEW**

*   **Context/Background:** Cyber threats and attacks are increasingly sophisticated, affecting individuals, small businesses, and large organizations. To address these threats, it is crucial for employees to understand cyber security fundamentals and learn how to handle malware attacks effectively. This training aims to equip employees with the necessary knowledge and skills to protect the organization's digital assets.
*   **Project Goal:** By the end of this training, employees will be able to identify and handle malware attacks, understand the importance of cyber security, and recognize early warning signs of cyber threats.
*   **Duration:** Estimated 6 hours

**LEARNING OBJECTIVES**

*   Learners will be able to handle malware attacks happening in organization.
*   Learners will be able to identify and understand the types of malware and cyber attacks encountered in day-to-day work.
*   Learners will be able to recognize early warning signs of cyber threats and understand the impact of security breaches on business continuity.
*   Learners will be able to explain why cyber security is critical for organizations and understand the importance of data encryption, integrity, and availability.

**MODULE BREAKDOWN**

| Module | Delivery Mode | Learning Objectives | Topics | Recommended Strategy | Activities/Assessment | Duration |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Module 1: Introduction to Cyber Security | Self-paced eLearning | • Define basic cyber security concepts.  
• Explain why cyber security is critical for organizations.  
• Identify common types of malware and cyber attacks encountered in day-to-day work.  
• Recognize early warning signs of cyber threats.  
• Understand the impact of security breaches on business continuity. | • Definition of Cyber Security  
• Importance of Cyber Security  
• Cyber Security in the Digital World  
• Malware & Ransomware:  
  - Definition of malware and its types (viruses, worms, spyware, trojans).  
  - What is ransomware and how does it work?  
  - Consequences of malware and ransomware attacks. | A simulation explores the impact of a ransomware attack on a company's business continuity. Learners must identify the warning signs and take action to prevent the attack. Interactive scenarios guided the learner different cyber security scenarios, highlighting the importance of data encryption, integrity, and availability. | • Drag and drop cybersecurity concepts  
• Multiple-choice questions on cybersecurity basics. | 2 hour |
| Module 2: Types of Malware and Cyber Attacks | Self-paced eLearning | • Identify different types of malware and cyber attacks.  
• Explain the characteristics and consequences of each type of malware and cyber attack.  
• Recognize the early warning signs of malware and cyber attacks. | • Types of Malware and Cyber Attacks  
  - Viruses, Worms, Spyware, Trojans, and Ransomware  
  - Web-based attacks  
• Characteristics and Consequences of Each Type of Malware and Cyber Attack | A branching scenario allows learners to explore different types of malware and cyber attacks, identifying the characteristics and consequences of each. Interactive quizzes evaluate the learner's understanding of the different types of malware and cyber attacks. | • Activity: Identifying malware and cyber attacks  
• Quiz: Multiple-choice questions | 1.5 hour |
| Module 3: Cyber Security Fundamentals | Self-paced eLearning | • Explain the importance of confidentiality, integrity, and availability in cyber security.  
• Identify the measures to establish confidentiality, integrity, and availability. | • Confidentiality, Integrity, and Availability  
  - Definition and importance of each  
  - Measures to establish each | Interactive scenarios guided the learner through different cyber security scenarios, highlighting the importance of confidentiality, integrity, and availability. Case studies reveal the impact of security breaches on business continuity. | • Drag and drop cybersecurity concepts  
• Multiple-choice questions on cybersecurity basics. | 2 hour |
| Module 4: Prevention and Mitigation | Self-paced eLearning | • Explain the measures to prevent and mitigate malware and cyber attacks.  
• Identify the best practices for maintaining a secure digital environment. | • Prevention and Mitigation Measures  
  - Data encryption, firewalls, antivirus software, and regular software updates  
  - Best practices for maintaining a secure digital environment. | A simulation explores the impact of a malware attack on a company's digital environment. Learners must identify the measures to prevent and mitigate the attack. Interactive quizzes evaluate the learner's understanding of the prevention and mitigation measures. | • Activity: Identifying prevention and mitigation measures  
• Quiz: Multiple-choice questions | 1.5 hour |
| Module 5: Incident Response | Self-paced eLearning | • Explain the importance of incident response in cyber security.  
• Identify the measures to respond to a malware or cyber attack. | • Incident Response Measures  
  - Identifying and containing the breach  
  - Reporting and communicating the breach  
  - Recovering and restoring systems and data | A branching scenario allows learners to explore different incident response scenarios, identifying the measures to respond to a malware or cyber attack. Interactive quizzes evaluate the learner's understanding of the incident response measures. | • Activity: Identifying incident response measures  
• Quiz: Multiple-choice questions | 1.5 hour |

**KNOWLEDGE CHECK**

*   **Delivery Mode:** Self-paced eLearning
*   **Learning Objectives:** Assess understanding of cyber security fundamentals, types of malware and cyber attacks, and measures to prevent and mitigate malware and cyber attacks.
*   **Topics:** Cyber security fundamentals, types of malware and cyber attacks, prevention and mitigation measures, and incident response measures.
*   **Recommended Strategy:** Quiz Format
*   **Activities/Assessment:** Multiple-choice quiz with scenario-based questions.
*   **Duration:** 30 minutes

**SUMMARY & CONCLUSION**

*   **Delivery Mode:** Self-paced eLearning
*   **Learning Objectives:** Review key concepts and summarize the importance of cyber security in the digital world.
*   **Topics:** Summary of key concepts and takeaways.
*   **Recommended Strategy:** Recap points
*   **Activities/Assessment:** Certificate of Completion.
*   **Duration:** 15 minutes

**INSTRUCTIONAL STRATEGY**

*   **Pedagogy:** Level 2 – Medium Interactivity (Level 1 + animations + interactions)
*   **Interactivity:** Click and Reveal, Tabs Interaction, Accordion Interaction, Hotspots
*   **Media:** Text with supporting icons, Infographics, Process flow diagrams, Photographic visuals, Charts and graphs, Tables

**ASSESSMENT STRATEGY**

*   **Formative:** Knowledge checks throughout the course to evaluate learner understanding.
*   **Summative:** Final assessment at the end of the course to evaluate learner understanding of cyber security fundamentals, types of malware and cyber attacks, and measures to prevent and mitigate malware and cyber attacks.
*   **Criteria:** Pass/fail criteria based on learner performance on the final assessment.

**TECHNICAL SPECIFICATIONS**

*   **LMS:** SCORM 1.2
*   **Devices:** Desktop/Laptop, Tablet

Module 1: Introduction to AI
Screen 1.1 Title: What is Artificial Intelligence?

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Definition of AI • History of AI • Key milestones in AI development • Importance of AI in various industries | "Welcome to this module on Introduction to AI. AI is a field of computer science that focuses on creating intelligent machines that can perform tasks that typically require human intelligence. The history of AI dates back to the 1950s when the term was first coined by John McCarthy. Since then, AI has made significant progress with many key milestones, including the development of the first AI program, ELIZA, in 1966. Today, AI is used in various industries, including healthcare, finance, and education. Let's explore this further." | Graphics: Image of John McCarthy, founder of AI, with a brief timeline of AI milestones in the background.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Please ensure the animation of the timeline is smooth and engaging.

Screen 1.2 Title: History of AI

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• ELIZA, the first AI program • Turing Test • Expert Systems | "Let's take a closer look at the history of AI. One of the earliest AI programs was ELIZA, developed in 1966. ELIZA was a natural language processing program that could simulate a conversation with a human. The Turing Test, developed in 1950, is another significant milestone in AI. It's a measure of a machine's ability to exhibit intelligent behavior equivalent to, or indistinguishable from, that of a human. Expert Systems, developed in the 1970s, are another example of AI's early progress." | Graphics: Image of ELIZA, with a brief description of its capabilities, followed by an image of the Turing Test and Expert Systems.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Please ensure the images are high-quality and relevant to the topic.

Module 2: AI Fundamentals
Topic: Machine Learning vs Deep Learning
Topic: Machine Learning vs Deep Learning
Screen 2.1 Title: Introduction to Machine Learning

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Machine Learning is a subset of Artificial Intelligence. • It involves training algorithms to learn from data and make predictions. • Machine Learning has two types: Supervised and Unsupervised Learning. • Supervised Learning involves training algorithms on labeled data, while Unsupervised Learning involves training algorithms on unlabeled data. | Welcome to Module 2: AI Fundamentals, where we'll explore the exciting world of Machine Learning. As we discussed in the previous module, AI is a broad field that encompasses various subfields, including Machine Learning. Machine Learning is a key aspect of AI that enables algorithms to learn from data and make predictions. This process involves training algorithms on a dataset, and the goal is to improve the algorithm's performance over time. In this module, we'll delve into the world of Machine Learning, starting with its basics. | Graphics: Illustration of a brain with gears and lights, symbolizing Machine Learning. The background is a blurred image of a cityscape, representing the vast possibilities of AI.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the visual is engaging and conveys the idea of Machine Learning as a subset of AI.

Screen 2.2 Title: Machine Learning vs Deep Learning

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Machine Learning is often confused with Deep Learning, but they are not the same. • Deep Learning is a type of Machine Learning that involves training neural networks with multiple layers. • Neural networks are a key component of Deep Learning, and they're inspired by the structure and function of the human brain. • Deep Learning is particularly useful for tasks like image and speech recognition. | As we explored the basics of Machine Learning, it's essential to differentiate it from another related concept: Deep Learning. While Machine Learning is a broad field, Deep Learning is a specific type of Machine Learning that involves training neural networks with multiple layers. Neural networks are a key component of Deep Learning, and they're inspired by the structure and function of the human brain. In this section, we'll explore the differences between Machine Learning and Deep Learning. | Graphics: Illustration of a neural network with multiple layers, representing Deep Learning. The background is a blurred image of a brain, emphasizing the connection to the human brain.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the visual is clear and conveys the idea of neural networks as a key component of Deep Learning.

Screen 2.3 Title: Supervised Learning

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Supervised Learning involves training algorithms on labeled data. • The goal of Supervised Learning is to enable the algorithm to make predictions on new, unseen data. • Supervised Learning is commonly used for tasks like image classification and sentiment analysis. • Example of Supervised Learning: training a model to recognize handwritten digits. | In this section, we'll explore Supervised Learning, a key type of Machine Learning. Supervised Learning involves training algorithms on labeled data, where the correct output is already known. The goal of Supervised Learning is to enable the algorithm to make predictions on new, unseen data. This type of Learning is commonly used for tasks like image classification and sentiment analysis. Let's look at an example: training a model to recognize handwritten digits. | Graphics: Illustration of a handwritten digit with a red box around it, representing the labeled data. The background is a blurred image of a keyboard, emphasizing the connection to machine learning models.   Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the visual is clear and conveys the idea of labeled data in Supervised Learning.

Screen 2.4 Title: Unsupervised Learning

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Unsupervised Learning involves training algorithms on unlabeled data. • The goal of Unsupervised Learning is to enable the algorithm to discover patterns or relationships in the data. • Unsupervised Learning is commonly used for tasks like clustering and dimensionality reduction. • Example of Unsupervised Learning: training a model to group customers based on their purchasing behavior. | In this section, we'll explore Unsupervised Learning, another key type of Machine Learning. Unsupervised Learning involves training algorithms on unlabeled data, where the correct output is unknown. The goal of Unsupervised Learning is to enable the algorithm to discover patterns or relationships in the data. This type of Learning is commonly used for tasks like clustering and dimensionality reduction. Let's look at an example: training a model to group customers based on their purchasing behavior. | Graphics: Illustration of a cluster of customers with different purchasing behaviors, representing the unlabeled data. The background is a blurred image of a shopping mall, emphasizing the connection to customer behavior.   Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the visual is clear and conveys the idea of unlabeled data in Unsupervised Learning.

Module 3: AI Applications
Topic: NLP
Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Natural Language Processing (NLP)

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Definition of NLP: NLP is a subfield of AI that deals with the interaction between computers and humans in natural language. • Importance of NLP: NLP has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, sentiment analysis, and language translation. • Types of NLP: There are three primary types of NLP: Text Classification, Sentiment Analysis, and Named Entity Recognition. • Applications of NLP: NLP is widely used in chatbots, virtual assistants, and language translation software. | NLP is a crucial aspect of AI that enables computers to understand and interpret human language. In today's digital age, NLP has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, sentiment analysis, and language translation. One of the key benefits of NLP is its ability to improve customer experience through personalized interactions. However, NLP also has its challenges, such as handling nuances of human language and dealing with ambiguity. There are three primary types of NLP: Text Classification, Sentiment Analysis, and Named Entity Recognition. Text Classification involves categorizing text into predefined categories, while Sentiment Analysis aims to determine the emotional tone of the text. Named Entity Recognition, on the other hand, identifies specific entities in the text, such as names, locations, and organizations. NLP is widely used in chatbots, virtual assistants, and language translation software. For instance, virtual assistants like Siri and Alexa use NLP to understand voice commands and respond accordingly. Similarly, language translation software relies on NLP to translate text from one language to another. | Graphics: An infographic illustrating the definition and importance of NLP, along with its various applications.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the infographic is visually appealing and easy to understand.

Screen 3.2 Title: Text Classification

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Definition of Text Classification: Text Classification is a type of NLP that involves categorizing text into predefined categories. • Types of Text Classification: There are two primary types of Text Classification: Supervised and Unsupervised Learning. • Applications of Text Classification: Text Classification is widely used in spam filtering, sentiment analysis, and topic modeling. • Examples of Text Classification: Email classification, sentiment analysis of customer reviews, and topic modeling of news articles. | Text Classification is a fundamental aspect of NLP that enables computers to categorize text into predefined categories. There are two primary types of Text Classification: Supervised and Unsupervised Learning. Supervised Learning involves training the model on labeled data, while Unsupervised Learning involves identifying patterns in unlabeled data. Text Classification has numerous applications in various industries, including spam filtering, sentiment analysis, and topic modeling. For instance, spam filtering systems use Text Classification to categorize emails as spam or not spam. Similarly, sentiment analysis systems use Text Classification to determine the emotional tone of customer reviews. | Graphics: A flowchart illustrating the process of Text Classification, including Supervised and Unsupervised Learning.   Navigation: Click Next to continue.   Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the flowchart is clear and easy to follow.

Screen 3.3 Title: Sentiment Analysis

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Definition of Sentiment Analysis: Sentiment Analysis is a type of NLP that involves determining the emotional tone of text. • Importance of Sentiment Analysis: Sentiment Analysis has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, marketing, and social media analysis. • Types of Sentiment Analysis: There are two primary types of Sentiment Analysis: Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based. • Applications of Sentiment Analysis: Sentiment Analysis is widely used in customer service, marketing, and social media analysis. | Sentiment Analysis is a critical aspect of NLP that enables computers to determine the emotional tone of text. Sentiment Analysis has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, marketing, and social media analysis. One of the key benefits of Sentiment Analysis is its ability to improve customer experience through personalized interactions. However, Sentiment Analysis also has its challenges, such as handling nuances of human language and dealing with ambiguity. There are two primary types of Sentiment Analysis: Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based. Rule-Based Sentiment Analysis involves using predefined rules to determine the emotional tone of text, while Machine Learning-based Sentiment Analysis involves training the model on labeled data. Sentiment Analysis is widely used in customer service, marketing, and social media analysis. For instance, customer service systems use Sentiment Analysis to determine the emotional tone of customer reviews and respond accordingly. | Graphics: A bar chart illustrating the process of Sentiment Analysis, including Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based approaches.   Navigation: Click Next to continue.   Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the bar chart is clear and easy to understand.

Screen 3.4 Title: Named Entity Recognition

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Definition of Named Entity Recognition: Named Entity Recognition is a type of NLP that involves identifying specific entities in text. • Importance of Named Entity Recognition: Named Entity Recognition has numerous applications in various industries, including information retrieval, question answering, and text summarization. • Types of Named Entity Recognition: There are two primary types of Named Entity Recognition: Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based. • Applications of Named Entity Recognition: Named Entity Recognition is widely used in information retrieval, question answering, and text summarization. | Named Entity Recognition is a fundamental aspect of NLP that enables computers to identify specific entities in text. Named Entity Recognition has numerous applications in various industries, including information retrieval, question answering, and text summarization. One of the key benefits of Named Entity Recognition is its ability to improve information retrieval through accurate entity identification. However, Named Entity Recognition also has its challenges, such as handling ambiguity and dealing with out-of-vocabulary words. There are two primary types of Named Entity Recognition: Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based. Rule-Based Named Entity Recognition involves using predefined rules to identify specific entities, while Machine Learning-based Named Entity Recognition involves training the model on labeled data. Named Entity Recognition is widely used in information retrieval, question answering, and text summarization. For instance, search engines use Named Entity Recognition to identify specific entities in search queries and provide accurate results. | Graphics: A diagram illustrating the process of Named Entity Recognition, including Rule-Based and Machine Learning-based approaches.   Navigation: Click Next to continue.   Additional Note to PG: Ensure that the diagram is clear and easy to follow.

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Summary of NLP: NLP is a subfield of AI that deals with the interaction between computers and humans in natural language. • Importance of NLP: NLP has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, sentiment analysis, and language translation. • Future of NLP: NLP is a rapidly evolving field with numerous opportunities for growth and development. | In conclusion, NLP is a critical aspect of AI that enables computers to understand and interpret human language. NLP has numerous applications in various industries, including customer service, sentiment analysis, and language translation. As the field of NLP continues to evolve, it is essential to stay up-to-date with the latest advancements and techniques. By doing so, we can unlock the full potential of NLP and improve the way we interact with computers. | Graphics: A screenshot of a chatbot interface, illustrating the application of NLP in customer service. Module 4: AI Challenges and Limitations
Topic: Bias in AI Systems
Screen 4.1 Title: Understanding Bias in AI Systems

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Bias in AI systems can lead to unfair decision-making. • Different types of bias exist in AI systems. • Bias can be intentional or unintentional. • Bias can affect the performance of AI systems. | Narration: "As we continue to integrate AI into our daily lives, it's essential to understand the challenges and limitations of AI systems. One significant challenge is bias in AI systems. Bias can lead to unfair decision-making, which can have severe consequences. There are different types of bias in AI systems, including intentional and unintentional bias. Intentional bias is when developers intentionally design the system to favor certain groups, while unintentional bias occurs when the system learns patterns from biased data. Bias can also affect the performance of AI systems, leading to inaccurate predictions and poor decision-making. In this module, we will explore the concept of bias in AI systems and its impact on AI applications." | Graphics: A picture of a scale with a tilted balance, representing the concept of bias.  Navigation: Click Next to learn more about the types of bias in AI systems.  Additional Note to PG: Use a simple and clear font to ensure readability.

Screen 4.2 Title: Types of Bias in AI Systems

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Intentional bias is when developers intentionally design the system to favor certain groups. • Unintentional bias occurs when the system learns patterns from biased data. • Confirmation bias is when the system only considers information that confirms its existing beliefs. • Anchoring bias is when the system relies too heavily on the first piece of information it receives. | Narration: "There are different types of bias in AI systems, including intentional and unintentional bias. Intentional bias is when developers intentionally design the system to favor certain groups. This can be done to achieve a specific goal or to manipulate the outcome of the system. Unintentional bias, on the other hand, occurs when the system learns patterns from biased data. This can happen when the training data is biased or when the system is not properly designed. Additionally, confirmation bias and anchoring bias can also affect the performance of AI systems. Confirmation bias occurs when the system only considers information that confirms its existing beliefs, while anchoring bias occurs when the system relies too heavily on the first piece of information it receives." | Graphics: A diagram showing the different types of bias in AI systems.  Navigation: Click Next to learn more about the causes of bias in AI systems.  Additional Note to PG: Use a flowchart to illustrate the different types of bias.

Screen 4.3 Title: Causes of Bias in AI Systems

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Biased data can lead to biased AI systems. • Lack of diversity in the development team can result in biased AI systems. • Insufficient testing and validation can lead to biased AI systems. • Poor data quality and labeling can result in biased AI systems. | Narration: "So, what causes bias in AI systems? Biased data can lead to biased AI systems. This is because the system learns patterns from the data it is trained on. If the data is biased, the system will also be biased. Additionally, lack of diversity in the development team can result in biased AI systems. This is because different people bring different perspectives and experiences to the development process. If the team is not diverse, it may not consider the needs and perspectives of all stakeholders. Insufficient testing and validation can also lead to biased AI systems. This is because the system may not be thoroughly tested and validated to ensure it is fair and unbiased. Finally, poor data quality and labeling can result in biased AI systems. This is because the data may not be accurate or reliable, leading to biased patterns and conclusions." | Graphics: A picture of a data set with a red "X" marked through it, representing biased data.  Navigation: Click Next to learn more about the effects of bias in AI systems.  Additional Note to PG: Use a warning symbol to indicate the risks of biased data.

Screen 4.4 Title: Effects of Bias in AI Systems

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Bias in AI systems can lead to unfair decision-making. • Bias can affect the performance of AI systems. • Bias can result in inaccurate predictions and poor decision-making. • Bias can lead to social and economic disparities. | Narration: "So, what are the effects of bias in AI systems? Bias in AI systems can lead to unfair decision-making. This is because the system may make decisions based on biased patterns and conclusions. Bias can also affect the performance of AI systems, leading to inaccurate predictions and poor decision-making. Additionally, bias can result in social and economic disparities. This is because the system may favor certain groups over others, leading to unequal treatment and outcomes." | Graphics: A picture of a scale with a tilted balance, representing unfair decision-making.  Navigation: Click Next to learn more about mitigating bias in AI systems.  Additional Note to PG: Use a red "X" marked through a balance scale to indicate unfair decision-making.

Screen 4.5 Title: Mitigating Bias in AI Systems

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Use diverse and representative data sets. • Implement fair and transparent algorithms. • Regularly test and validate AI systems. • Ensure diverse and inclusive development teams. | Narration: "So, how can we mitigate bias in AI systems? One way is to use diverse and representative data sets. This can help ensure that the system learns patterns from accurate and reliable data. Another way is to implement fair and transparent algorithms. This can help ensure that the system makes decisions based on clear and consistent rules. Additionally, regularly testing and validating AI systems can help identify and address bias. Finally, ensuring diverse and inclusive development teams can help ensure that the system is designed to meet the needs and perspectives of all stakeholders." | Graphics: A picture of a diverse group of people working together, representing inclusive development teams.  Navigation: Click Next to complete the module.  Additional Note to PG: Use a green checkmark to indicate successful mitigation of bias.

Module 5: AI Ethics and Governance
Screen 5.1 Title: AI Ethics Fundamentals

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• AI ethics refers to the principles and values that guide the development and use of AI systems. • These principles ensure that AI systems are transparent, accountable, and fair. • AI ethics is essential for building trust in AI and promoting its adoption in various industries. | As we explore the world of AI, it's essential to consider the ethics surrounding its development and use. AI ethics is about establishing principles and values that guide the creation and deployment of AI systems. This ensures that AI systems are transparent, accountable, and fair. By following these principles, we can build trust in AI and promote its adoption in various industries. For instance, AI-powered healthcare systems must prioritize patient confidentiality and data privacy. Similarly, AI-driven financial systems must ensure fairness and transparency in decision-making processes. As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's crucial to establish clear guidelines and regulations to prevent potential harm and promote responsible AI development. | Graphics: AI ethics framework illustration with key principles highlighted.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure the AI ethics framework illustration is interactive, allowing learners to hover over each principle to learn more.

Screen 5.2 Title: Principles of AI Ethics

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Transparency: AI systems should be transparent in their decision-making processes and data usage. • Accountability: AI systems must be accountable for their actions and decisions. • Fairness: AI systems must ensure fairness and equity in their decision-making processes. | As we delve deeper into the principles of AI ethics, it's essential to understand the importance of transparency, accountability, and fairness. Transparency ensures that AI systems are open and honest in their decision-making processes, while accountability holds AI systems responsible for their actions. Fairness, on the other hand, guarantees that AI systems treat individuals equally and without bias. These principles are critical in building trust in AI and promoting its adoption in various industries. For instance, AI-powered hiring systems must ensure fairness and equity in their decision-making processes to prevent bias against certain groups. Similarly, AI-driven financial systems must be transparent in their decision-making processes to prevent unexpected outcomes. | Graphics: Infographic illustrating the three principles of AI ethics (transparency, accountability, and fairness).  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure the infographic is interactive, allowing learners to click on each principle to learn more.

Screen 5.3 Title: Role of Regulation in AI

On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes
• Data protection: AI systems must ensure the protection of sensitive data and personal information. • Intellectual property: AI systems must respect intellectual property rights and avoid copyright infringement. • Regulatory compliance: AI systems must comply with relevant regulations and laws. | As AI becomes increasingly integrated into our lives, it's essential to establish clear regulations and guidelines to prevent potential harm and promote responsible AI development. Data protection ensures that sensitive data and personal information are safeguarded from unauthorized access. Intellectual property rights must be respected to prevent copyright infringement. Regulatory compliance is critical in ensuring that AI systems adhere to relevant laws and regulations. For instance, AI-powered healthcare systems must comply with HIPAA regulations to protect patient data. Similarly, AI-driven financial systems must comply with relevant financial regulations to prevent unexpected outcomes. | Graphics: Diagram illustrating the importance of data protection, intellectual property, and regulatory compliance in AI development.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: Ensure the diagram is interactive, allowing learners to hover over each concept to learn more.

Additional Note to PG: Ensure the conclusion page is interactive and engaging, allowing learners to review key concepts and principles of AI ethics in a timely manner.

# STORYBOARD — Cyber Security For Employees

Module 1: Introduction to Malware Topic: Definition of Malware Screen 1.1 Title: What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Malware is a type of malicious software • It is designed to harm or exploit a computer system • Malware can be spread through various means, including email, infected software downloads, and exploited vulnerabilities | The term "malware" is short for "malicious software." It's a type of software that's designed to harm or exploit a computer system. Malware can come in many forms, including viruses, worms, trojans, and spyware. To understand how malware works, let's start with its definition. | Graphics: A simple icon representing malware with a red "X" through it. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: The icon should be prominent and easily recognizable. |

Screen 1.2 Title: Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Viruses: Self-replicating malware that attaches to other programs and files • Worms: Malware that can spread from system to system without user interaction • Trojans: Disguised malware that appears legitimate but carries malicious intent | Malware comes in many forms, including viruses, worms, and trojans. Viruses are self-replicating malware that attach to other programs and files, while worms can spread from system to system without user interaction. Trojans, on the other hand, appear to be legitimate software but carry malicious intent. | Graphics: A diagram showing the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: The diagram should be clear and easy to understand. |

Screen 1.3 Title: Consequences of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Data theft and loss • System crashes and downtime • Financial losses and reputational damage | Malware can have severe consequences, including data theft and loss, system crashes and downtime, and financial losses and reputational damage. It's essential to understand the risks associated with malware to take the necessary precautions. | Graphics: A visual representation of the consequences of malware, such as a crashed computer or a data breach. |

Screen 1.4 Title: Early Warning Signs of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Unexplained system crashes • Slow system performance • Pop-up ads and notifications | Malware can exhibit various warning signs, including unexplained system crashes, slow system performance, and pop-up ads and notifications. Being aware of these signs can help you detect and prevent malware infections. | Graphics: A visual representation of the early warning signs of malware, such as a crashed computer or a slow system performance. |

Screen 1.5 Title: Importance of Malware Security

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Protecting sensitive data • Preventing system crashes and downtime • Maintaining business continuity | Malware security is crucial for protecting sensitive data, preventing system crashes and downtime, and maintaining business continuity. By understanding the importance of malware security, you can take the necessary steps to safeguard your systems and data. | Graphics: A visual representation of the importance of malware security, such as a secure computer or a business operating smoothly. |

Screen 1.6 Title: Impact of Malware on Business Continuity

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Data loss and theft • System downtime and crashes • Financial losses and reputational damage | Malware can have a significant impact on business continuity, including data loss and theft, system downtime and crashes, and financial losses and reputational damage. Module 3: Malware Detection and Prevention Topic: Malware Detection Methods Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Malware Detection Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Signature-based detection • Behavior-based detection • Anomaly-based detection | As we discussed earlier, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity. There are several methods used to detect malware, and each has its strengths and weaknesses. Signature-based detection involves identifying known malware patterns, while behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by the malware. Anomaly-based detection, on the other hand, looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. | Graphics: An infographic showing the three detection methods, with arrows connecting them to highlight their relationships. The infographic should be colorful and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Make sure to use simple, concise language to explain these complex concepts. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Signature-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Definition of signature-based detection • How signature-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Signature-based detection is a widely used method that involves identifying known malware patterns, or "signatures." These signatures are compared to a database of known malware patterns to determine if a file or program is malicious. While this method is effective, it can be outsmarted by advanced malware that uses polymorphism or code obfuscation to evade detection. | Graphics: A diagram showing how signature-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how signature-based detection works. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Behavior-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Definition of behavior-based detection • How behavior-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by a program or file, rather than its signature. This method involves monitoring system calls, API calls, and other system activity to determine if a program is behaving in a suspicious manner. While this method is more effective against advanced malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how behavior-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how behavior-based detection works. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Anomaly-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Definition of anomaly-based detection • How anomaly-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Anomaly-based detection looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. This method involves monitoring system activity and network traffic to determine if there are any unusual patterns that may indicate a malicious activity. While this method is effective against unknown malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how anomaly-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how anomaly-based detection works. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Choosing the Right Detection Method

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Factors to consider when choosing a detection method • Advantages and disadvantages of each method • Example scenario | When choosing a malware detection method, there are several factors to consider, including the type of malware you are trying to detect, the level of false positives you are willing to tolerate, and the complexity of the detection method. Each detection method has its advantages and disadvantages, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. For example, if you are trying to detect advanced malware, behavior-based detection may be the best choice. | Graphics: A table showing the advantages and disadvantages of each detection method, with columns for each method. The table should be clear and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate the factors to consider when choosing a detection method. |

Screen 3.6 Title: Conclusion

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes | | • Summary of key points • Final thoughts on malware detection and prevention | In conclusion, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity, and there are several methods used to detect malware. Each method has its strengths and weaknesses, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. By understanding the different malware detection methods and how they work, you can make an informed decision about which method is best for your organization. | Graphics: A summary slide showing the key points of the module, with a simple diagram to illustrate the concepts. The slide should be clear and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate the key points of the module. |

In the event of a malware incident, the first step is to identify the incident and contain it to prevent further damage. # COURSE OVERVIEW
The purpose of this eLearning course is to provide an in-depth understanding of Generative AI, covering its fundamentals, applications, challenges, and ethics.

| Module 3 | Self-paced | Understand AI applications | Topic: NLP <br> Topic: Text Classification <br> Topic: Sentiment Analysis <br> Topic: Named Entity Recognition | Strategy A: Interactive simulations <br> Strategy B: Gamification | Activity A: Quizzes <br> Activity B: Case studies | 1 hour |

=============================================================================
Module 1: Introduction to Malware
Topic: Definition of Malware
=============================================================================

Screen 1.1 Title: What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Malware stands for “Malicious Software”.<br>• Malware is designed to gain access or installed into the computer without the consent of the user.| The term 'malware' refers to a broad category of malicious software that can compromise the security and integrity of computer systems. Malware is often spread through email attachments, downloads, or infected software. It can have devastating effects on an organization, including data breaches, compromised sensitive information, and system downtime. Let's explore what makes malware so destructive and how it can impact an organization. Malware can be spread through various means, including email attachments, downloads, and infected software. It can also be embedded in software updates or patches. The consequences of malware attacks can be severe, resulting in financial losses, damaged reputation, and compromised data. As an employee, it's essential to understand the risks associated with malware and take proactive steps to prevent its spread. | • Visual description: A simple, clean layout with a dark blue background and white text. The title "What is Malware?" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with a red "X" symbol over it is used to represent malware. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.2 Title: Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Adware<br>• Spyware<br>• Virus<br>• Worms<br>• Trojan Horse | Adware, spyware, viruses, worms, and Trojan horses are all types of malware that can compromise computer systems. Adware displays unwanted advertisements, while spyware tracks user activity and sends it to third-party servers. Viruses modify or delete system files, causing system crashes or data loss. Worms replicate themselves, spreading malware across networks. Trojan horses disguise themselves as legitimate software, allowing hackers to access sensitive information. These types of malware can be spread through various means, including email attachments, downloads, and infected software. | • Visual description: A simple, clean layout with a light blue background and white text. The title "Types of Malware" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A diagram is used to show the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.3 Title: Adware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Adware displays unwanted advertisements.<br>• Adware is often bundled with free software downloads.<br>• Adware can be difficult to remove. | Adware is a type of malware that displays unwanted advertisements on your computer. It's often bundled with free software downloads, making it difficult to detect. Adware can be challenging to remove, and it can compromise your browsing experience. | • Visual description: A screen with a lot of pop-up ads and advertisements on it. The title "Adware" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with adware is used to represent the concept. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.4 Title: Spyware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Spyware tracks user activity and sends it to third-party servers.<br>• Spyware can be spread through email attachments or downloads.<br>• Spyware can compromise sensitive information. | Spyware is a type of malware that tracks user activity and sends it to third-party servers. It can be spread through email attachments or downloads, making it difficult to detect. Spyware can compromise sensitive information, including passwords and credit card numbers. | • Visual description: A screen with a spyware icon on it. The title "Spyware" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with spyware is used to represent the concept. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.5 Title: Virus

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Viruses modify or delete system files.<br>• Viruses can cause system crashes or data loss.<br>• Viruses can be spread through email attachments or downloads. | Viruses are a type of malware that modify or delete system files, causing system crashes or data loss. They can be spread through email attachments or downloads, making it difficult to detect. Viruses can compromise the integrity of your computer system. | • Visual description: A screen with a virus icon on it. The title "Virus" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with a virus is used to represent the concept. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.6 Title: Worms

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Worms replicate themselves.<br>• Worms can spread malware across networks.<br>• Worms can compromise network resources. | Worms are a type of malware that replicate themselves, spreading malware across networks. They can compromise network resources, including bandwidth and storage. Worms can cause significant damage to a computer system. | • Visual description: A screen with a worm icon on it. The title "Worms" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with a worm is used to represent the concept. The on-screen text is listed in a bullet-point format with a consistent font and size. |

Screen 1.7 Title: Trojan Horse

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Trojan horses disguise themselves as legitimate software.<br>• Trojan horses can allow hackers to access sensitive information.<br>• Trojan horses can compromise system security. | Trojan horses are a type of malware that disguise themselves as legitimate software, allowing hackers to access sensitive information. They can compromise system security, including passwords and credit card numbers. Trojan horses can cause significant damage to a computer system. | • Visual description: A screen with a Trojan horse icon on it. The title "Trojan Horse" is displayed prominently at the top of the screen. A picture of a computer with a Trojan horse is used to represent the concept. It's essential to understand malware to protect computer systems. Malware can be spread through various means, including email attachments, downloads, and infected software. By understanding the types of malware and how they can compromise computer systems, you can take proactive steps to prevent their spread. | • Visual description: A screen with a conclusion message on it. Module 2: Understanding Malware Risks
Topic: Risk Factors
=============================================================================

Screen 2.1 Title: Human Error and Malware Risks

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Human error can lead to malware infections.<br>• Clicking on suspicious links or downloading attachments from unknown sources can compromise your computer.<br>• Lack of awareness and training can make employees more susceptible to phishing attacks. | Human error is a significant risk factor in malware infections. When employees are not aware of the potential threats, they may unintentionally download malware or click on suspicious links. This can compromise the entire organization's network and lead to significant financial losses. As an employee, it's essential to be cautious and report any suspicious activity to the IT department. Let's explore the different types of human errors that can lead to malware risks. | • A pie chart will be displayed, highlighting the percentage of malware infections caused by human error.<br>• A screenshot of a phishing email will be shown, emphasizing the importance of being cautious when clicking on links or downloading attachments.<br>• An image of an employee reporting suspicious activity to the IT department will be displayed, encouraging users to report any anomalies. |

Screen 2.2 Title: Phishing and Social Engineering

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Phishing attacks can be sophisticated and difficult to identify.<br>• Social engineering tactics, such as pretexting and baiting, can trick employees into divulging sensitive information.<br>• Malware-laden emails and attachments can be disguised as legitimate communications. | Phishing attacks are becoming increasingly sophisticated, making it challenging for employees to identify them. Social engineering tactics, such as pretexting and baiting, can manipulate employees into divulging sensitive information. It's essential to be cautious when receiving emails or attachments, especially if they seem suspicious or unsolicited. Let's explore some examples of phishing attacks and social engineering tactics. | • A screenshot of a phishing email will be displayed, highlighting the warning signs of a phishing attack.<br>• An image of a social engineer attempting to trick an employee will be shown, emphasizing the importance of being cautious when dealing with unknown individuals.<br>• A diagram illustrating the different types of phishing attacks will be displayed, providing a clear understanding of the risks. |

Screen 2.3 Title: Unpatched Vulnerabilities

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Unpatched vulnerabilities in software and systems can leave organizations exposed to malware attacks.<br>• Failing to update software and systems can create an entry point for malware to spread.<br>• Regular updates and patches can help prevent malware infections. | Unpatched vulnerabilities in software and systems can create an entry point for malware to spread, putting the entire organization at risk. It's essential to regularly update software and systems to prevent malware infections. Let's explore some examples of unpatched vulnerabilities and how they can be exploited by malware. | • A diagram illustrating the different types of vulnerabilities will be displayed, highlighting the risks associated with unpatched vulnerabilities.<br>• A screenshot of a software update will be shown, emphasizing the importance of regular updates and patches.<br>• An image of an employee updating their software will be displayed, encouraging users to regularly update their systems. |

| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Human error, phishing attacks, and unpatched vulnerabilities are significant risk factors in malware infections.<br>• Regular updates and patches can help prevent malware infections.<br>• Employee awareness and training are crucial in preventing malware risks. | Let's summarize the key risk factors we've discussed so far. Human error, phishing attacks, and unpatched vulnerabilities are significant risk factors in malware infections. Regular updates and patches can help prevent malware infections. Employee awareness and training are crucial in preventing malware risks. As an employee, it's essential to be cautious and report any suspicious activity to the IT department. | • A pie chart will be displayed, highlighting the percentage of malware infections caused by human error, phishing attacks, and unpatched vulnerabilities.<br>• A screenshot of an employee reporting suspicious activity will be shown, emphasizing the importance of employee awareness and training.<br>• An image of a secure system will be displayed, encouraging users to regularly update their software and systems. |

Module 3: Identifying and Preventing Malware
Topic: Warning Signs
=============================================================================

Screen 3.1 Title: Recognizing Malware Warning Signs

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • **Unusual system behavior**<br>• **Unexplained data loss or corruption**<br>• **Slow system performance**<br>• **Suspicious emails or attachments** | Malware can manifest in various ways, but one common sign is unusual system behavior. This can include slow performance, errors, or crashes. Another warning sign is unexplained data loss or corruption. Be cautious of suspicious emails or attachments, as these can be used to spread malware. Remember, prevention is key. Always keep your operating system and software up to date. Use antivirus software and firewalls to protect your system. | • A screenshot of a Windows desktop with a frozen cursor and error messages popping up.<br>• A simple icon-based layout with navigation buttons to explore each warning sign in more detail.<br>• A visual representation of a system crash, with a red "X" marked through a computer screen. |

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • **Slow performance**<br>• **Error messages**<br>• **Crashes** | Unusual system behavior can be a sign of malware. Slow performance, error messages, and crashes are all common indicators. To prevent malware, ensure your operating system and software are up to date. Use antivirus software and firewalls to protect your system. Remember, prevention is key. Be cautious of suspicious emails or attachments. | • A video clip of a computer slowing down, with error messages popping up and the system freezing.<br>• An interactive graph showing the relationship between system performance and malware infection.<br>• A series of screenshots showcasing different types of error messages. |

Use antivirus software and firewalls to protect your system. Remember, prevention is key. Be cautious of suspicious emails or attachments. | • A series of screenshots showcasing different types of data loss or corruption.<br>• A video clip of a computer crashing, with a red "X" marked through a screen.<br>• An interactive diagram illustrating the impact of data loss or corruption on a system. |

Module 4: Responding to Malware Attacks
=============================================================================

Screen 4.1 Title: Understanding Incident Response

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Incident response is the process of identifying and containing malware.<br>• It involves isolating affected systems and minimizing downtime.<br>• Effective incident response requires a well-planned strategy and timely action.<br>• Incident response teams should be trained to handle malware attacks. | As we've learned, malware attacks can have devastating consequences for an organization. In this section, we'll explore the importance of incident response and containment. When a malware attack occurs, every minute counts. The sooner you respond, the less damage you'll suffer. A well-planned incident response strategy can make all the difference. | • Visual: An image of a computer screen with a red "Alert" icon and a clock ticking in the background.<br>• Layout: A simple, clean layout with a blue background and white text.<br>• Navigation: A button labeled "Next" that leads to the next screen. |

Screen 4.2 Title: Identifying Affected Systems

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Identify affected systems and networks.<br>• Determine the scope of the malware attack.<br>• Isolate affected systems to prevent further damage.<br>• Contain the malware to prevent it from spreading. | When a malware attack occurs, it's essential to identify the affected systems and networks as quickly as possible. This will help you determine the scope of the attack and contain the malware before it spreads. Remember, every minute counts. The sooner you isolate the affected systems, the less damage you'll suffer. | • Visual: An image of a computer network diagram with red flags marking affected systems.<br>• Layout: A simple, clean layout with a yellow background and black text.<br>• Navigation: A button labeled "Next" that leads to the next screen. |

Screen 4.3 Title: Containing Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Contain the malware to prevent it from spreading.<br>• Isolate affected systems and networks.<br>• Prevent further damage by containing the malware.<br>• Use antivirus software and firewalls to prevent malware from spreading. | Containing malware is a critical step in incident response. By isolating affected systems and networks, you can prevent further damage and prevent the malware from spreading. Remember to use antivirus software and firewalls to prevent malware from spreading in the first place. | • Visual: An image of a firewalls and antivirus software icons with a red "Blocked" icon.<br>• Layout: A simple, clean layout with a green background and white text.<br>• Navigation: A button labeled "Next" that leads to the next screen. |

| :--- | :--- | :--- |

By containing the malware quickly and using backup systems, you can restore data and services as quickly as possible. Remember to communicate with stakeholders and affected parties and review and update incident response plans. | • Visual: An image of a clock ticking with a green "Restored" icon in the background.<br>• Layout: A simple, clean layout with a blue background and white text.<br>• Navigation: A button labeled "Next" that leads to the next screen. |

# Project ID: 891fa8a7-a6d7-4561-86ac-c94f8b987388 - Title: download (8)
# PROJECT INFORMATION
- **Project Title:** Training Program For IT
- **Trainers:** 
- **Instructor / AI Assistant:** 
- **Target Audience:** 
- **Course Overview:** Design Document for Cyber Security For Employees — Self-paced eLearning

# COURSE OVERVIEW
This self-paced eLearning course is designed to educate employees on cyber security fundamentals, focusing on malware prevention, detection, and response. The course consists of five modules, each covering essential topics and activities to ensure learners understand and apply the knowledge.

## Module 1: Malware Fundamentals
### Module Details
| Module | Delivery Mode | Learning Objectives | Topics | Recommended Strategy | Activities/Assessment | Duration |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Module 1: Malware Fundamentals | Self-paced eLearning | • Define basic malware concepts.<br>• Identify common types of malware (viruses, worms, spyware, trojans).<br>• Explain the differences between malware and other types of cyber threats.<br>• Recognize the risks associated with malware attacks. | • Definition of Malware<br>  - Types of malware (viruses, worms, spyware, trojans)<br>  - Malware vs. other cyber threats<br>  - Risks associated with malware attacks | A simulation explores the consequences of malware attacks on an organization's operations and reputation. Interactive scenarios guided the learner through identifying and preventing malware infections. The learning path concludes with a hands-on drag-and-drop exercise matching malware concepts to defense strategies. | • Drag and drop malware concepts<br>• Multiple-choice questions on malware basics. | 1 hour |

## Module 2: Malware Prevention and Mitigation
### Module Details

# STORYBOARD — Cyber Security For Employees
Module 1: Introduction to Malware
Topic: Definition of Malware
Screen 1.1 Title: What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Malware is a type of malicious software • It is designed to harm or exploit a computer system • Malware can be spread through various means, including email, infected software downloads, and exploited vulnerabilities | The term "malware" is short for "malicious software." It's a type of software that's designed to harm or exploit a computer system. Malware can come in many forms, including viruses, worms, trojans, and spyware. To understand how malware works, let's start with its definition. | Graphics: A simple icon representing malware with a red "X" through it.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The icon should be prominent and easily recognizable. |

Screen 1.2 Title: Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Viruses: Self-replicating malware that attaches to other programs and files • Worms: Malware that can spread from system to system without user interaction • Trojans: Disguised malware that appears legitimate but carries malicious intent | Malware comes in many forms, including viruses, worms, and trojans. Viruses are self-replicating malware that attach to other programs and files, while worms can spread from system to system without user interaction. Trojans, on the other hand, appear to be legitimate software but carry malicious intent. | Graphics: A diagram showing the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The diagram should be clear and easy to understand. |

Screen 1.3 Title: Consequences of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Data theft and loss • System crashes and downtime • Financial losses and reputational damage | Malware can have severe consequences, including data theft and loss, system crashes and downtime, and financial losses and reputational damage. It's essential to understand the risks associated with malware to take the necessary precautions. | Graphics: A visual representation of the consequences of malware, such as a crashed computer or a data breach. |

Screen 1.4 Title: Early Warning Signs of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Unexplained system crashes • Slow system performance • Pop-up ads and notifications | Malware can exhibit various warning signs, including unexplained system crashes, slow system performance, and pop-up ads and notifications. Module 3: Malware Detection and Prevention
Topic: Malware Detection Methods
Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Malware Detection Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Signature-based detection • Behavior-based detection • Anomaly-based detection | As we discussed earlier, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity. There are several methods used to detect malware, and each has its strengths and weaknesses. Signature-based detection involves identifying known malware patterns, while behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by the malware. Anomaly-based detection, on the other hand, looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. | Graphics: An infographic showing the three detection methods, with arrows connecting them to highlight their relationships. The infographic should be colorful and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Make sure to use simple, concise language to explain these complex concepts. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Signature-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of signature-based detection • How signature-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Signature-based detection is a widely used method that involves identifying known malware patterns, or "signatures." These signatures are compared to a database of known malware patterns to determine if a file or program is malicious. While this method is effective, it can be outsmarted by advanced malware that uses polymorphism or code obfuscation to evade detection. | Graphics: A diagram showing how signature-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how signature-based detection works. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Behavior-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of behavior-based detection • How behavior-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by a program or file, rather than its signature. This method involves monitoring system calls, API calls, and other system activity to determine if a program is behaving in a suspicious manner. While this method is more effective against advanced malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how behavior-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how behavior-based detection works. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Anomaly-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of anomaly-based detection • How anomaly-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Anomaly-based detection looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. This method involves monitoring system activity and network traffic to determine if there are any unusual patterns that may indicate a malicious activity. While this method is effective against unknown malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how anomaly-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how anomaly-based detection works. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Choosing the Right Detection Method

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Factors to consider when choosing a detection method • Advantages and disadvantages of each method • Example scenario | When choosing a malware detection method, there are several factors to consider, including the type of malware you are trying to detect, the level of false positives you are willing to tolerate, and the complexity of the detection method. Each detection method has its advantages and disadvantages, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. For example, if you are trying to detect advanced malware, behavior-based detection may be the best choice. | Graphics: A table showing the advantages and disadvantages of each detection method, with columns for each method. The table should be clear and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate the factors to consider when choosing a detection method. |

Screen 3.6 Title: Conclusion

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Summary of key points • Final thoughts on malware detection and prevention | In conclusion, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity, and there are several methods used to detect malware. Each method has its strengths and weaknesses, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. By understanding the different malware detection methods and how they work, you can make an informed decision about which method is best for your organization. | Graphics: A summary slide showing the key points of the module, with a simple diagram to illustrate the concepts. The slide should be clear and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate the key points of the module. |

Module 5: Malware Response and Recovery
Topic: Malware Response and Recovery Methods
Screen 5.1 Title: Understanding Malware Response and Recovery Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Malware response and recovery are critical components of cybersecurity.  • They involve identifying and mitigating malware threats, and restoring systems and data to a secure state.  • Effective malware response and recovery require a well-planned strategy and regular testing.  • This module will cover common malware response and recovery methods. | Malware response and recovery are critical components of cybersecurity. They involve identifying and mitigating malware threats, and restoring systems and data to a secure state. Effective malware response and recovery require a well-planned strategy and regular testing. In this module, we will cover common malware response and recovery methods. These methods include incident response, disaster recovery, and business continuity planning. By understanding these methods, you will be better equipped to respond to malware threats and minimize their impact. | Graphics: An image of a person responding to a malware incident, with a laptop in the background displaying a malware warning.  Navigation: Click Next to continue to the next screen.  Additional Note to PG: Please ensure that the image is high-quality and visually appealing. |

Screen 5.2 Title: Incident Response

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Incident response is the process of responding to and containing malware incidents.  • It involves identifying and containing the incident, and restoring systems and data to a secure state.  • Effective incident response requires a well-planned strategy and regular testing.  • This includes identifying the incident, containing it, and eradicating the malware. | Incident response is the process of responding to and containing malware incidents. It involves identifying and containing the incident, and restoring systems and data to a secure state. Effective incident response requires a well-planned strategy and regular testing. In the event of a malware incident, the first step is to identify the incident and contain it to prevent further damage. This includes isolating the affected systems and networks, and preventing further access to the malware. | Graphics: An image of a network diagram showing a malware incident being contained.  Navigation: Click Next to continue to the next screen.  Additional Note to PG: Please ensure that the image is clear and easy to understand. |

Screen 5.3 Title: Disaster Recovery

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Disaster recovery is the process of restoring systems and data to a secure state after a malware incident.  • It involves restoring systems and data from backups, and ensuring that the systems are secure and up-to-date.  • Effective disaster recovery requires a well-planned strategy and regular testing.  • This includes restoring systems and data, and ensuring that the systems are secure and up-to-date. | Disaster recovery is the process of restoring systems and data to a secure state after a malware incident. It involves restoring systems and data from backups, and ensuring that the systems are secure and up-to-date. Effective disaster recovery requires a well-planned strategy and regular testing. In the event of a malware incident, the next step is to restore systems and data from backups. This includes restoring the systems to a secure state, and ensuring that the systems are up-to-date and secure. | Graphics: An image of a person restoring systems and data from backups, with a laptop in the background displaying a backup software.  Navigation: Click Next to continue to the next screen.  Additional Note to PG: Please ensure that the image is high-quality and visually appealing. |
