Module 1: Introduction to Malware
Topic: Definition of Malware
Screen 1.1 Title: What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Malware is a type of malicious software • It is designed to harm or exploit a computer system • Malware can be spread through various means, including email, infected software downloads, and exploited vulnerabilities | The term "malware" is short for "malicious software." It's a type of software that's designed to harm or exploit a computer system. Malware can come in many forms, including viruses, worms, trojans, and spyware. To understand how malware works, let's start with its definition. | Graphics: A simple icon representing malware with a red "X" through it.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The icon should be prominent and easily recognizable. |

Screen 1.2 Title: Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Viruses: Self-replicating malware that attaches to other programs and files • Worms: Malware that can spread from system to system without user interaction • Trojans: Disguised malware that appears legitimate but carries malicious intent | Malware comes in many forms, including viruses, worms, and trojans. Viruses are self-replicating malware that attach to other programs and files, while worms can spread from system to system without user interaction. Trojans, on the other hand, appear to be legitimate software but carry malicious intent. | Graphics: A diagram showing the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The diagram should be clear and easy to understand. |

It's essential to understand the risks associated with malware to take the necessary precautions. | Graphics: A visual representation of the consequences of malware, such as a crashed computer or a data breach. |

Module 3: Malware Detection and Prevention
Topic: Malware Detection Methods
Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Malware Detection Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Signature-based detection • Behavior-based detection • Anomaly-based detection | As we discussed earlier, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity. There are several methods used to detect malware, and each has its strengths and weaknesses. Signature-based detection involves identifying known malware patterns, while behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by the malware. Anomaly-based detection, on the other hand, looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. | Graphics: An infographic showing the three detection methods, with arrows connecting them to highlight their relationships. The infographic should be colorful and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Make sure to use simple, concise language to explain these complex concepts. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Signature-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of signature-based detection • How signature-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Signature-based detection is a widely used method that involves identifying known malware patterns, or "signatures." These signatures are compared to a database of known malware patterns to determine if a file or program is malicious. While this method is effective, it can be outsmarted by advanced malware that uses polymorphism or code obfuscation to evade detection. | Graphics: A diagram showing how signature-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how signature-based detection works. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Behavior-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of behavior-based detection • How behavior-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by a program or file, rather than its signature. This method involves monitoring system calls, API calls, and other system activity to determine if a program is behaving in a suspicious manner. While this method is more effective against advanced malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how behavior-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how behavior-based detection works. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Anomaly-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of anomaly-based detection • How anomaly-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Anomaly-based detection looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. This method involves monitoring system activity and network traffic to determine if there are any unusual patterns that may indicate a malicious activity. While this method is effective against unknown malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how anomaly-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how anomaly-based detection works. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Choosing the Right Detection Method

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |

With the increasing reliance on technology, the potential risks and threats to our digital information and systems are also rising. Screen 2.1 Title: What is a Virus?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • A virus is a type of malware designed to harm or exploit a computer system.<br>• Viruses can cause damage to files, slow down system performance, or even spread to other computers.<br>• Viruses are typically spread through email attachments, infected software downloads, or infected USB drives.<br>• Once a virus infects a computer, it can replicate itself and spread to other parts of the system. | A virus is a type of malware that is designed to harm or exploit a computer system. It can cause damage to files, slow down system performance, or even spread to other computers. Viruses are typically spread through email attachments, infected software downloads, or infected USB drives. Once a virus infects a computer, it can replicate itself and spread to other parts of the system. | • Visual description: A simple diagram showing a computer system with a virus infecting it. The virus is represented by a red circle with a white "V" inside.<br>• Layout details: The OST is displayed in a clean, white font with a blue background. The diagram is placed below the OST, taking up most of the screen space.<br>• Navigation instructions: The user can click on the diagram to explore it in more detail. |

Screen 2.2 Title: Examples of Viruses

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Computer viruses, such as the I Love You virus, which spread rapidly in the early 2000s.<br>• File viruses, which infect specific types of files, such as Word documents or Excel spreadsheets.<br>• Boot viruses, which infect a computer's boot sector and spread to other parts of the system.<br>• Logic bombs, which are designed to cause harm to a computer system at a specific time or under specific conditions. | Computer viruses, such as the I Love You virus, spread rapidly in the early 2000s. File viruses infect specific types of files, such as Word documents or Excel spreadsheets. Boot viruses infect a computer's boot sector and spread to other parts of the system. Logic bombs are designed to cause harm to a computer system at a specific time or under specific conditions. | • Visual description: An image showing a computer screen with a virus alert popping up. The OST is displayed in a clean, white font with a blue background.<br>• Layout details: The image takes up most of the screen space, with the OST displayed above it in a smaller font size.<br>• Navigation instructions: The user can click on the image to explore it in more detail. |

Module 3: Cyber Security Best Practices
Topic: Strong Passwords
=============================================================================

Screen 3.1 Title: Why Strong Passwords Are Important

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Weak passwords can be easily guessed by hackers.<br>• Strong passwords protect your personal and professional data.<br>• Passwords should be unique for each account.<br>• Passwords should be changed every 60-90 days. | As we discussed earlier, cyber threats can come from anywhere, and weak passwords can be an easy target for hackers. Strong passwords, on the other hand, can protect your personal and professional data. It's essential to create unique passwords for each account and change them regularly to maintain your online security. | • Visualize a lock icon on a computer screen with a red "X" marked through it, indicating a weak password.<br>• Use a simple, clean layout with a password strength meter in the background, displaying a gradual progression from weak to strong.<br>• Include a navigation button to proceed to the next topic: "Phishing and Spear Phishing." |

Screen 3.2 Title: Creating Strong Passwords

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Use a combination of uppercase and lowercase letters.<br>• Include numbers and special characters.<br>• Avoid using easily guessable information.<br>• Use a password manager to generate and store unique passwords. | Creating strong passwords requires a combination of letters, numbers, and special characters. Avoid using easily guessable information, such as your name, birthdate, or common words. Consider using a password manager to generate and store unique passwords for each account. | • Illustrate a password creation interface with a keyboard and a password strength meter in the background, displaying a gradual progression from weak to strong.<br>• Use a simple, clean layout with a password generator button in the foreground, displaying a random password as an example.<br>• Include a navigation button to review the previous topic: "Why Strong Passwords Are Important." |

Don't use the same password for multiple accounts, and avoid using easily guessable information. Module 4: Cyber Security Tools and Technologies
Topic: Firewalls
=============================================================================

**Screen 4.1 Title:** Introduction to Firewalls

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Definition of Firewalls<br>• Importance of Firewalls in Cyber Security<br>• Types of Firewalls | Welcome to this module on cyber security tools and technologies. In this section, we will be discussing firewalls, which play a crucial role in protecting our computer systems from unauthorized access. A firewall is essentially a network security system that monitors and controls incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predetermined security rules. There are two main types of firewalls: hardware firewalls and software firewalls. Hardware firewalls are physical devices installed between the internet and a private network, while software firewalls are programs running on a computer or server. | • Visual description: A simple diagram of a hardware firewall with arrows showing incoming and outgoing traffic.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise heading with bullet points for easy reading.<br>• Navigation instructions: A "Next" button to proceed to the next screen. |

**Screen 4.2 Title:** Types of Firewalls

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Hardware Firewalls<br>• Software Firewalls<br>• Next-Generation Firewalls | A hardware firewall is a physical device that is installed between the internet and a private network. It acts as a barrier between the two, monitoring and controlling incoming and outgoing traffic. A software firewall, on the other hand, is a program running on a computer or server that monitors and controls network traffic. Next-generation firewalls are advanced firewalls that incorporate additional security features such as intrusion prevention and sandboxing. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the difference between hardware and software firewalls.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise heading with bullet points for easy reading.<br>• Navigation instructions: A "Next" button to proceed to the next screen. |

**Screen 4.3 Title:** Benefits of Firewalls

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Protection from Unauthorized Access<br>• Prevention of Malware and Viruses<br>• Improved Network Security | Firewalls provide several benefits, including protection from unauthorized access, prevention of malware and viruses, and improved network security. By blocking incoming and outgoing traffic, firewalls prevent hackers from gaining access to our computer systems. They also prevent malware and viruses from entering our systems, reducing the risk of data breaches and other security threats. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the benefits of firewalls.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise heading with bullet points for easy reading.<br>• Navigation instructions: A "Next" button to proceed to the next screen. |

**Screen 4.4 Title:** How Firewalls Work

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Packet Filtering<br>• Stateful Inspection<br>• Deep Packet Inspection | Firewalls work by inspecting incoming and outgoing network traffic based on predetermined security rules. There are three main methods of inspection: packet filtering, stateful inspection, and deep packet inspection. Packet filtering involves checking the source and destination IP addresses of incoming traffic. Stateful inspection involves checking the context of the traffic, including the source and destination IP addresses, as well as the type of traffic. Deep packet inspection involves checking the contents of the traffic, including the data being transmitted. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the different methods of inspection.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise heading with bullet points for easy reading.<br>• Navigation instructions: A "Next" button to proceed to the next screen. |

**Screen 4.5 Title:** Conclusion

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Summary of Key Points<br>• Final Thoughts | In conclusion, firewalls are an essential tool in protecting our computer systems from unauthorized access and malware. They provide several benefits, including protection from unauthorized access, prevention of malware and viruses, and improved network security. By understanding how firewalls work and the different types of firewalls available, we can make informed decisions about our network security. | • Visual description: A summary of key points with a call-to-action to take the next step.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise heading with bullet points for easy reading.<br>• Navigation instructions: A "Next" button to proceed to the next screen or a "Complete" button to complete the module. |

Screen 5.1 Title: Importance of Incident Response Plan

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • A well-planned incident response plan helps minimize damage and downtime.<br>• It ensures a coordinated response from all stakeholders.<br>• It reduces the risk of data breaches and financial losses. | In a rapidly evolving cyber threat landscape, having a well-planned incident response plan is crucial. It helps organizations to respond quickly and effectively to security incidents, minimizing damage and downtime. A good incident response plan ensures a coordinated response from all stakeholders, including IT, management, and communication teams. This approach reduces the risk of data breaches and financial losses. Without a plan, organizations risk facing significant consequences, including reputational damage and financial losses. | • Visualize a company's IT infrastructure, with a red alert sign indicating a security incident.<br>• Use a simple, easy-to-understand diagram to illustrate the importance of incident response planning.<br>• Include a picture of a team of professionals working together to respond to an incident. |

Screen 5.2 Title: Steps Involved in Responding to a Cyber Security Incident

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Containment: Isolate the affected system or network to prevent further damage.<br>• Eradication: Remove the threat or malware from the system or network.<br>• Recovery: Restore normal operations and ensure business continuity.<br>• Post-Incident Activities: Conduct a thorough analysis and implement corrective actions. | Responding to a cyber security incident involves several key steps. The first step is containment, which involves isolating the affected system or network to prevent further damage. Eradication is the next step, where the threat or malware is removed from the system or network. Recovery is crucial, as it involves restoring normal operations and ensuring business continuity. Finally, post-incident activities, such as conducting a thorough analysis and implementing corrective actions, are essential to prevent similar incidents in the future. | • Use a flowchart or diagram to illustrate the steps involved in responding to a cyber security incident.<br>• Include pictures or icons to represent each step, such as a lock for containment and a trash can for eradication.<br>• Use colors to highlight the importance of each step, such as red for containment and green for recovery. |

The IT team is responsible for responding to incidents, containing and eradicating threats, and recovering systems. Management oversees incident response efforts, makes strategic decisions, and communicates with stakeholders. The communication team coordinates communication with stakeholders, including employees, customers, and media. | • Use a table or matrix to illustrate the roles and responsibilities of each team.<br>• Include pictures or icons to represent each team, such as a computer for the IT team and a megaphone for the communication team.<br>• Use colors to highlight the importance of each team, such as blue for IT and red for management. |

| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Enhances incident response skills and knowledge.<br>• Improves communication and coordination among teams.<br>• Reduces response time and minimizes damage.<br>• Identifies and addresses weaknesses in the incident response plan. | Regular training and exercises are essential to ensure that incident response teams are prepared to respond effectively to security incidents. These activities enhance incident response skills and knowledge, improve communication and coordination among teams, and reduce response time and minimize damage. Additionally, regular training and exercises help identify and address weaknesses in the incident response plan. | • Use a diagram or infographic to illustrate the benefits of regular training and exercises.<br>• Include pictures or icons to represent each benefit, such as a clock for reducing response time and a shield for minimizing damage.<br>• Use colors to highlight the importance of each benefit, such as green for improving communication and red for identifying weaknesses. |

=============================================================================

**Screen 1.1 Title:** What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Malware is a type of malicious software<br>• It is designed to harm or exploit a computer system<br>• Malware can be spread through various means, including email, infected software downloads, and exploited vulnerabilities | The term "malware" is short for "malicious software." It's a type of software that's designed to harm or exploit a computer system. Malware can come in many forms, including viruses, worms, trojans, and spyware. To understand how malware works, let's start with its definition. | **Graphics:** A simple icon representing malware with a red "X" through it.<br><br>**Navigation:** Click Next to continue.<br><br>**Additional Note to PG:** The icon should be prominent and easily recognizable. |

**Screen 1.2 Title:** Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Viruses: Self-replicating malware that attaches to other programs and files<br>• Worms: Malware that can spread from system to system without user interaction<br>• Trojans: Disguised malware that appears legitimate but carries malicious intent | Malware comes in many forms, including viruses, worms, and trojans. Viruses are self-replicating malware that attach to other programs and files, while worms can spread from system to system without user interaction. Trojans, on the other hand, appear to be legitimate software but carry malicious intent. | **Graphics:** A diagram showing the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon.<br><br>**Navigation:** Click Next to continue.<br><br>**Additional Note to PG:** The diagram should be clear and easy to understand. |

Module 3: Malware Detection and Prevention
Topic: Malware Detection Methods
=============================================================================

Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Malware Detection Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Signature-based detection<br>• Behavior-based detection<br>• Anomaly-based detection | As we discussed earlier, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity. There are several methods used to detect malware, and each has its strengths and weaknesses. Signature-based detection involves identifying known malware patterns, while behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by the malware. Anomaly-based detection, on the other hand, looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. | **Graphics:** An infographic showing the three detection methods, with arrows connecting them to highlight their relationships. The infographic should be colorful and easy to understand. **Navigation:** Click Next to continue. **Additional Note to PG:** Make sure to use simple, concise language to explain these complex concepts. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Signature-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Definition of signature-based detection<br>• How signature-based detection works<br>• Advantages and disadvantages | Signature-based detection is a widely used method that involves identifying known malware patterns, or "signatures." These signatures are compared to a database of known malware patterns to determine if a file or program is malicious. While this method is effective, it can be outsmarted by advanced malware that uses polymorphism or code obfuscation to evade detection. | **Graphics:** A diagram showing how signature-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. **Navigation:** Click Next to continue. **Additional Note to PG:** Use a simple example to illustrate how signature-based detection works. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Behavior-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Definition of behavior-based detection<br>• How behavior-based detection works<br>• Advantages and disadvantages | Behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by a program or file, rather than its signature. This method involves monitoring system calls, API calls, and other system activity to determine if a program is behaving in a suspicious manner. While this method is more effective against advanced malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | **Graphics:** A diagram showing how behavior-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. **Navigation:** Click Next to continue. **Additional Note to PG:** Use a simple example to illustrate how behavior-based detection works. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Anomaly-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Definition of anomaly-based detection<br>• How anomaly-based detection works<br>• Advantages and disadvantages | Anomaly-based detection looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. This method involves monitoring system activity and network traffic to determine if there are any unusual patterns that may indicate a malicious activity. While this method is effective against unknown malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | **Graphics:** A diagram showing how anomaly-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. **Navigation:** Click Next to continue. **Additional Note to PG:** Use a simple example to illustrate how anomaly-based detection works. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Choosing the Right Detection Method

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Factors to consider when choosing a detection method<br>• Advantages and disadvantages of each method<br>• Example scenario | When choosing a malware detection method, there are several factors to consider, including the type of malware you are trying to detect, the level of false positives you are willing to tolerate, and the complexity of the detection method. Each detection method has its advantages and disadvantages, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. For example, if you are trying to detect advanced malware, behavior-based detection may be the best choice. | **Graphics:** A table showing the advantages and disadvantages of each detection method, with columns for each method. The table should be clear and easy to understand. **Navigation:** Click Next to continue. **Additional Note to PG:** Use a simple example to illustrate the factors to consider when choosing a detection method. |

Screen 3.6 Title: Conclusion

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Summary of key points<br>• Final thoughts on malware detection and prevention | In conclusion, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity, and there are several methods used to detect malware. Each method has its strengths and weaknesses, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. By understanding the different malware detection methods and how they work, you can make an informed decision about which method is best for your organization. | **Graphics:** A summary slide showing the key points of the module, with a simple diagram to illustrate the concepts. Module 1: Understanding Malware
Topic: Definition of Malware
=============================================================================

**Screen 1.1 Title:** What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Malware stands for "Malicious Software".<br>• It is designed to gain access or installed into the computer without the consent of the user.<br>• Malware performs unwanted tasks in the host computer for the benefit of a third party. | The term "malware" may seem complex, but it's actually quite simple. Malware is short for "malicious software", which means that it's designed to harm or disrupt your computer. Imagine you received a package in the mail with a mysterious object inside. You wouldn't know what it was or what it did, would you? That's kind of like what malware does to your computer. It sneaks in and starts causing problems without your knowledge or permission. | • A simple, clean page with a blue background and a large title "What is Malware?"<br>• A small image of a computer with a red "X" marked through it to represent malware<br>• A call-to-action button "Learn More" in the bottom right corner |

**Screen 1.2 Title:** History of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Malware has been around since the early days of computing.<br>• The first malware was created in the 1970s by a group of university students.<br>• Since then, malware has evolved and become more sophisticated. | As computers became more popular, so did the idea of creating malicious software. The first malware was created in the 1970s by a group of university students who wanted to see how far they could push the limits of what was possible. They created a simple virus that would replicate itself and cause problems for other users. Since then, malware has evolved and become more sophisticated, with new types of malware emerging all the time. | • A timeline graphic showing key milestones in the history of malware, with images and brief descriptions<br>• A small image of a university campus to represent the origins of malware<br>• A call-to-action button "Learn More" in the bottom right corner |

| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Use strong, unique passwords for all email accounts.<br>• Avoid using easily guessable information such as names or birthdays.<br>• Use a password manager to store and generate complex passwords. | When it comes to password management, it's essential to use strong, unique passwords for all email accounts. Enable 2FA for all email accounts and use an authenticator app or SMS to receive verification codes. Use PGP or S/MIME encryption protocols to encrypt emails and ensure that all email clients support encryption. This can help prevent unauthorized access to sensitive information. | • Use an infographic to illustrate the process of email encryption.<br>• Highlight the benefits of using PGP or S/MIME encryption protocols.<br>• Provide a link to a reputable email encryption tool. |

Module 3: Identifying and Reporting Phishing Attacks
Topic: Phishing Tactics and Techniques
=============================================================================

Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Phishing Tactics and Techniques

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Phishing is a type of social engineering attack that tricks victims into revealing sensitive information.<br>• Phishing attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message.<br>• Phishing tactics include spoofing, pretexting, and baiting.<br>• Phishing attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed. | Phishing is a type of social engineering attack that tricks victims into revealing sensitive information. This can include passwords, credit card numbers, or other personal data. Phishing attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message, and can be highly targeted or widely distributed. In this section, we'll explore the different tactics and techniques used in phishing attacks. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the different types of phishing attacks, with arrows connecting each type to a description of the tactic.<br>• Layout details: A clean and simple layout with plenty of white space to make it easy to read and understand.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about phishing tactics. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Spoofing: A Common Phishing Tactic

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Spoofing involves creating a fake email or message that appears to come from a trusted sender.<br>• Spoofing can be used to trick victims into revealing sensitive information or clicking on malicious links.<br>• Spoofing attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message.<br>• Spoofing attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed. | Spoofing is a common phishing tactic that involves creating a fake email or message that appears to come from a trusted sender. This can include fake emails from banks, credit card companies, or other organizations that you trust. Spoofing attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message, and can be highly targeted or widely distributed. | • Visual description: A screenshot of a fake email that appears to come from a trusted sender, with a red X marked through it to indicate that it is a phishing attack.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise layout with a bold heading to draw attention to the spoofing tactic.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about pretexting. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Pretexting: A Phishing Tactic that Tricks Victims

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Pretexting involves creating a fake scenario or story to trick victims into revealing sensitive information.<br>• Pretexting attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message.<br>• Pretexting attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed.<br>• Pretexting attacks can be difficult to detect. | Pretexting is a phishing tactic that involves creating a fake scenario or story to trick victims into revealing sensitive information. This can include fake emails or messages that appear to come from a trusted sender, or fake phone calls that appear to come from a trusted organization. Pretexting attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message, and can be highly targeted or widely distributed. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the different types of pretexting attacks, with arrows connecting each type to a description of the tactic.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise layout with a bold heading to draw attention to the pretexting tactic.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about baiting. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Baiting: A Phishing Tactic that Tricks Victims with a Reward

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Baiting involves creating a fake reward or incentive to trick victims into revealing sensitive information.<br>• Baiting attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message.<br>• Baiting attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed.<br>• Baiting attacks can be difficult to detect. | Baiting is a phishing tactic that involves creating a fake reward or incentive to trick victims into revealing sensitive information. This can include fake emails or messages that appear to come from a trusted sender, or fake phone calls that appear to come from a trusted organization. Baiting attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message, and can be highly targeted or widely distributed. | • Visual description: A screenshot of a fake email that appears to come from a trusted sender, with a red X marked through it to indicate that it is a phishing attack.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise layout with a bold heading to draw attention to the baiting tactic.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about recognizing phishing attacks. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Recognizing Phishing Attacks

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Phishing attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed.<br>• Phishing attacks can be carried out via email, phone, or text message.<br>• Phishing attacks can be difficult to detect.<br>• Recognizing phishing attacks is crucial to protecting sensitive information. | Recognizing phishing attacks is crucial to protecting sensitive information. Phishing attacks can be highly targeted or widely distributed, and can be carried out via email, phone, or text message. They can be difficult to detect, but there are some common signs that can indicate a phishing attack. | • Visual description: A diagram showing the common signs of a phishing attack, with arrows connecting each sign to a description of the tactic.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise layout with a bold heading to draw attention to the importance of recognizing phishing attacks.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about reporting phishing attacks. |

Screen 3.6 Title: Reporting Phishing Attacks

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Reporting phishing attacks is crucial to protecting sensitive information.<br>• Reporting phishing attacks can help prevent further attacks.<br>• Reporting phishing attacks can help identify vulnerabilities in the system.<br>• Reporting phishing attacks is a critical step in maintaining cybersecurity. | Reporting phishing attacks is a critical step in maintaining cybersecurity. Reporting phishing attacks can help prevent further attacks, identify vulnerabilities in the system, and protect sensitive information. If you suspect a phishing attack, it's essential to report it to the relevant authorities. | • Visual description: A screenshot of a reporting form, with a red X marked through it to indicate that it is a phishing attack.<br>• Layout details: A clear and concise layout with a bold heading to draw attention to the importance of reporting phishing attacks.<br>• Navigation instructions: A clear call to action to click on the next section to learn more about next steps. |

Module 4: Understanding Email Encryption
Topic: Email Encryption
=============================================================================

Screen 4.1 Title: Importance of Email Encryption

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Email encryption is crucial for protecting sensitive information in emails.<br>• It ensures that only authorized parties can read the content of encrypted emails.<br>• Email encryption prevents unauthorized access to confidential data. | Email encryption is a vital aspect of email security. It ensures that sensitive information remains confidential and protected from unauthorized access. Without email encryption, sensitive data can be easily intercepted and exploited by cyber attackers. As a result, email encryption is a must-have feature for organizations that handle sensitive information. | • Visualize a secure email encryption process with a locked padlock icon.<br>• Use a simple, clean background to avoid distractions.<br>• Display a call-out box with a key icon, highlighting the importance of email encryption. |

Screen 4.2 Title: Types of Email Encryption

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • PGP (Pretty Good Privacy) is a widely used email encryption standard.<br>• S/MIME (Secure/Multipurpose Internet Mail Extensions) is another popular email encryption protocol.<br>• These protocols ensure the confidentiality and integrity of email communications. | When it comes to email encryption, there are several types of protocols that can be used. Two popular options are PGP and S/MIME. PGP is a widely used standard that provides end-to-end encryption, while S/MIME is a more widely adopted protocol that offers a range of encryption options. Both protocols provide a high level of security and are widely used in the industry. | • Use a split-screen layout to compare and contrast PGP and S/MIME.<br>• Visualize a PGP key and an S/MIME certificate to illustrate the encryption process.<br>• Display a key icon next to each protocol to highlight their encryption capabilities. |

Screen 4.3 Title: Email Encryption Implementation

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Email encryption can be implemented through various methods, including server-side and client-side encryption.<br>• Organizations can also use email encryption gateways to encrypt and decrypt emails<br>• Email encryption can be configured to work with existing email systems. | Implementing email encryption requires careful planning and configuration. Organizations can use various methods to implement email encryption, including server-side and client-side encryption. Email encryption gateways can also be used to encrypt and decrypt emails, ensuring that sensitive information remains protected. | • Visualize a diagram showing the email encryption process, including the encryption and decryption steps.<br>• Display a checklist of implementation steps, including key management and certificate configuration.<br>• Use a call-out box to highlight the importance of key management in email encryption. |

Screen 4.4 Title: Email Encryption Benefits

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Email encryption provides confidentiality, integrity, and authenticity of email communications.<br>• It protects sensitive information from unauthorized access and interception.<br>• Email encryption also ensures compliance with data protection regulations. | Email encryption provides a range of benefits, including confidentiality, integrity, and authenticity of email communications. By encrypting emails, organizations can protect sensitive information from unauthorized access and interception. Email encryption also ensures compliance with data protection regulations, reducing the risk of data breaches and fines. | • Use a pie chart to illustrate the benefits of email encryption, highlighting confidentiality, integrity, and authenticity.<br>• Visualize a secure email encryption process with a locked padlock icon.<br>• Display a call-out box with a compliance icon, highlighting the importance of email encryption in data protection regulations. |

Screen 4.5 Title: Email Encryption Challenges

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Email encryption can be complex to implement and manage.<br>• Key management and certificate configuration can be challenging.<br>• Email encryption may require significant hardware and software investments. | Implementing and managing email encryption can be complex, requiring significant resources and expertise. Key management and certificate configuration can be challenging, and email encryption may require significant hardware and software investments. | • Use a diagram to illustrate the challenges of email encryption, highlighting key management and certificate configuration.<br>• Visualize a secure email encryption process with a locked padlock icon.<br>• Display a call-out box with a warning icon, highlighting the importance of careful planning and configuration. |

Screen 4.6 Title: Best Practices for Email Encryption

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Organizations should establish clear email encryption policies and procedures.<br>• Implement robust key management and certificate configuration processes.<br>• Regularly review and update email encryption configurations to ensure compliance with data protection regulations. | To ensure the effective implementation and management of email encryption, organizations should establish clear policies and procedures. Robust key management and certificate configuration processes should be implemented, and email encryption configurations should be regularly reviewed and updated to ensure compliance with data protection regulations. | • Use a checklist to illustrate best practices for email encryption, highlighting clear policies and procedures, key management, and regular reviews. |

Module 7: Incident Response and Recovery
Topic: Incident Response Process
=============================================================================

Screen 7.1 Title: Introduction to Incident Response

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • What is Incident Response?<br>• Importance of Incident Response<br>• Types of Incident Response (Identification, Containment, Eradication, Recovery) | The incident response process is a critical component of cybersecurity. It involves identifying, containing, eradicating, and recovering from cyber threats. The process is essential in minimizing the impact of a security breach and preventing further damage. Effective incident response requires a well-planned strategy, trained personnel, and the right tools. | • Visual description: A simple icon-based diagram illustrating the four stages of incident response. Layout details: The diagram should be placed on the center of the screen with a clean and simple background. Navigation instructions: The learner can click on each stage to learn more about it. |

Screen 7.2 Title: Identifying an Incident

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Signs of an Incident (Unusual Network Activity, Suspicious Emails, System Crashes)<br>• Identifying the Source of the Incident (Network Logs, System Logs, User Reports) | Identifying an incident is the first step in the incident response process. This involves recognizing the signs of an incident, such as unusual network activity, suspicious emails, or system crashes. Once an incident is identified, the next step is to determine its source. This can be done by analyzing network logs, system logs, or user reports. | • Visual description: An image of a network administrator monitoring system logs. Layout details: The image should be placed on the left side of the screen with a clean and simple background. Navigation instructions: The learner can click on a "Learn More" button to get more information on network logs and system logs. |

| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Containment Strategies (Isolating the Affected System, Blocking Network Traffic)<br>• Containment Tools (Firewalls, Intrusion Detection Systems) | Containment is the process of isolating the affected system or network to prevent further damage. This can be done by blocking network traffic or isolating the affected system. Containment tools, such as firewalls and intrusion detection systems, can be used to identify and block malicious activity. | • Visual description: A diagram illustrating a network with a firewall blocking malicious traffic. Layout details: The diagram should be placed on the center of the screen with a clean and simple background. Navigation instructions: The learner can click on a "Learn More" button to get more information on containment strategies and tools. |

This can be done by removing malware, patching vulnerabilities, or fixing configuration errors. Eradication tools, such as antivirus software and patch management tools, can be used to identify and remove malicious software or vulnerabilities. | • Visual description: An image of a system administrator patching a vulnerability. Recovery tools, such as backup and recovery software, can be used to identify and restore data or systems. | • Visual description: A diagram illustrating a system being restored from a backup. Module 8: Maintaining Cybersecurity Awareness
Topic: Maintaining Cybersecurity Awareness
=============================================================================

Screen 8.1 Title: Importance of Maintaining Cybersecurity Awareness

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Maintaining cybersecurity awareness is crucial in protecting organizations from cyber threats.<br>• Cybersecurity awareness helps employees identify and report potential threats.<br>• It also fosters a culture of cybersecurity within the organization. | Maintaining cybersecurity awareness is a critical aspect of protecting organizations from cyber threats. Cyber threats can come in many forms, including phishing, malware, and social engineering attacks. Cybersecurity awareness helps employees identify and report potential threats, which can prevent these attacks from occurring. Additionally, maintaining cybersecurity awareness fosters a culture of cybersecurity within the organization, where employees are empowered to take an active role in protecting the organization's assets. This can include reporting suspicious activity, using strong passwords, and avoiding suspicious email attachments. By maintaining cybersecurity awareness, employees can play a critical role in protecting the organization from cyber threats. | • Visual description: A photo of a group of employees working together, with a cityscape in the background.<br>• Layout details: The screen will have a clean and simple layout, with the title "Importance of Maintaining Cybersecurity Awareness" at the top, and the on-screen text below.<br>• Navigation instructions: The learner can proceed to the next screen by clicking the "Next" button at the bottom of the screen. |

Screen 8.2 Title: Potential Cybersecurity Threats

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Phishing attacks can occur through email, phone, or text messages.<br>• Malware can be installed on a device through infected software downloads or attachments.<br>• Social engineering attacks can occur through manipulation of employees into revealing sensitive information. | Phishing attacks can occur through email, phone, or text messages, and can be designed to trick employees into revealing sensitive information, such as login credentials or financial information. Malware can be installed on a device through infected software downloads or attachments, and can cause a range of problems, from slowing down the device to stealing sensitive information. Social engineering attacks can occur through manipulation of employees into revealing sensitive information, such as passwords or financial information. These attacks can be particularly effective, as they often rely on psychological manipulation rather than technical sophistication. | • Visual description: An infographic showing the different types of cybersecurity threats, including phishing, malware, and social engineering attacks.<br>• Layout details: The screen will have a simple and easy-to-read layout, with the title "Potential Cybersecurity Threats" at the top, and the on-screen text below.<br>• Navigation instructions: The learner can proceed to the next screen by clicking the "Next" button at the bottom of the screen. |

Screen 8.3 Title: Best Practices for Mitigating Cybersecurity Threats

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| • Employees should use strong passwords and avoid using the same password for multiple accounts.<br>• Employees should be cautious when clicking on links or downloading attachments from unknown sources.<br>• Employees should report any suspicious activity to the IT department. | Employees play a critical role in mitigating cybersecurity threats. By using strong passwords and avoiding the use of the same password for multiple accounts, employees can help prevent unauthorized access to sensitive information. Additionally, employees should be cautious when clicking on links or downloading attachments from unknown sources, as these can often be used to spread malware or phishing attacks. If employees notice any suspicious activity, they should report it to the IT department immediately. | • Visual description: A photo of an employee using a laptop, with a secure password manager open on the screen.<br>• Layout details: The screen will have a clean and simple layout, with the title "Best Practices for Mitigating Cybersecurity Threats" at the top, and the on-screen text below.<br>• Navigation instructions: The learner can proceed to the next screen by clicking the "Next" button at the bottom of the screen. |

Module 1: Introduction to Malware
Topic: Definition of Malware
Screen 1.1 Title: What is Malware?

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Malware is a type of malicious software • It is designed to harm or exploit a computer system • Malware can be spread through various means, including email, infected software downloads, and exploited vulnerabilities | The term "malware" is short for "malicious software." It's a type of software that's designed to harm or exploit a computer system. Malware can come in many forms, including viruses, worms, trojans, and spyware. To understand how malware works, let's start with its definition. | Graphics: A simple icon representing malware with a red "X" through it.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The icon should be prominent and easily recognizable. |

Screen 1.2 Title: Types of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Viruses: Self-replicating malware that attaches to other programs and files • Worms: Malware that can spread from system to system without user interaction • Trojans: Disguised malware that appears legitimate but carries malicious intent | Malware comes in many forms, including viruses, worms, and trojans. Viruses are self-replicating malware that attach to other programs and files, while worms can spread from system to system without user interaction. Trojans, on the other hand, appear to be legitimate software but carry malicious intent. | Graphics: A diagram showing the different types of malware, with each type represented by a distinct icon.  Navigation: Click Next to continue.  Additional Note to PG: The diagram should be clear and easy to understand. |

Screen 1.3 Title: Consequences of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Data theft and loss • System crashes and downtime • Financial losses and reputational damage | Malware can have severe consequences, including data theft and loss, system crashes and downtime, and financial losses and reputational damage. It's essential to understand the risks associated with malware to take the necessary precautions. | Graphics: A visual representation of the consequences of malware, such as a crashed computer or a data breach. |

Screen 1.4 Title: Early Warning Signs of Malware

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Unexplained system crashes • Slow system performance • Pop-up ads and notifications | Malware can exhibit various warning signs, including unexplained system crashes, slow system performance, and pop-up ads and notifications. Being aware of these signs can help you detect and prevent malware infections. | Graphics: A visual representation of the early warning signs of malware, such as a crashed computer or a slow system performance. |

Screen 1.5 Title: Importance of Malware Security

| • Protecting sensitive data • Preventing system crashes and downtime • Maintaining business continuity | Malware security is crucial for protecting sensitive data, preventing system crashes and downtime, and maintaining business continuity. By understanding the importance of malware security, you can take the necessary steps to safeguard your systems and data. | Graphics: A visual representation of the importance of malware security, such as a secure computer or a business operating smoothly. |

Screen 2.2 Title: Email Security Risks: Phishing

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Phishing is a type of email-based attack that tricks users into revealing sensitive information. • Spear phishing is a targeted form of phishing that targets specific individuals or groups. • Phishing attacks can lead to identity theft, financial loss, and reputational damage. • Be cautious of emails that ask for sensitive information or contain suspicious links. • Use two-factor authentication to add an extra layer of security. | Phishing is a type of email-based attack that tricks users into revealing sensitive information. Spear phishing is a targeted form of phishing that targets specific individuals or groups. Phishing attacks can lead to identity theft, financial loss, and reputational damage. Be cautious of emails that ask for sensitive information or contain suspicious links. Module 3: Malware Detection and Prevention
Topic: Malware Detection Methods
Screen 3.1 Title: Understanding Malware Detection Methods

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Signature-based detection • Behavior-based detection • Anomaly-based detection | As we discussed earlier, malware detection is a crucial aspect of cybersecurity. There are several methods used to detect malware, and each has its strengths and weaknesses. Signature-based detection involves identifying known malware patterns, while behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by the malware. Anomaly-based detection, on the other hand, looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. | Graphics: An infographic showing the three detection methods, with arrows connecting them to highlight their relationships. The infographic should be colorful and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Make sure to use simple, concise language to explain these complex concepts. |

Screen 3.2 Title: Signature-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of signature-based detection • How signature-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Signature-based detection is a widely used method that involves identifying known malware patterns, or "signatures." These signatures are compared to a database of known malware patterns to determine if a file or program is malicious. While this method is effective, it can be outsmarted by advanced malware that uses polymorphism or code obfuscation to evade detection. | Graphics: A diagram showing how signature-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how signature-based detection works. |

Screen 3.3 Title: Behavior-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of behavior-based detection • How behavior-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Behavior-based detection focuses on the actions taken by a program or file, rather than its signature. This method involves monitoring system calls, API calls, and other system activity to determine if a program is behaving in a suspicious manner. While this method is more effective against advanced malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how behavior-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how behavior-based detection works. |

Screen 3.4 Title: Anomaly-Based Detection

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Definition of anomaly-based detection • How anomaly-based detection works • Advantages and disadvantages | Anomaly-based detection looks for unusual patterns of behavior that may indicate a malware attack. This method involves monitoring system activity and network traffic to determine if there are any unusual patterns that may indicate a malicious activity. While this method is effective against unknown malware, it can also generate false positives if it is not properly configured. | Graphics: A diagram showing how anomaly-based detection works, with arrows and boxes to explain the process. The diagram should be clear and easy to follow. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate how anomaly-based detection works. |

Screen 3.5 Title: Choosing the Right Detection Method

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |
| • Factors to consider when choosing a detection method • Advantages and disadvantages of each method • Example scenario | When choosing a malware detection method, there are several factors to consider, including the type of malware you are trying to detect, the level of false positives you are willing to tolerate, and the complexity of the detection method. Each detection method has its advantages and disadvantages, and the right choice will depend on your specific needs. For example, if you are trying to detect advanced malware, behavior-based detection may be the best choice. | Graphics: A table showing the advantages and disadvantages of each detection method, with columns for each method. The table should be clear and easy to understand. Navigation: Click Next to continue. Additional Note to PG: Use a simple example to illustrate the factors to consider when choosing a detection method. |

Screen 3.6 Title: Conclusion

| On-Screen Text (OST) | Audio Narration | Visual Instructions & Developer Notes |

MODULE 4: Types of Malware

SECTION TOPICS VISUAL INSTRUCTIONS/DEVELOPER NOTES ON-SCREEN TEXT AUDIO NARRATION STATUS ACTIONS REQUIRED Intro Definition of Malware • Visual description: A simple, clean layout with a heading "Types of Malware". • Layout details: A series of icons representing different types of malware. • What is malware? • Malware stands for Malicious Software. • It is designed to gain access or installed into the computer without the consent of the user. The term malware refers to malicious software designed to harm or exploit a computer system. It can take many forms, including viruses, worms, spyware, and adware. Draft None Content Types of Malware • Visual description: A branching scenario with different types of malware, each with its own icon and description. • Types of Malware:   - Virus:     - A virus is a type of malware that replicates itself by attaching to other programs or files.   - Worm:     - A worm is a type of malware that can spread from computer to computer without human intervention.   - Spyware:     - Spyware is a type of malware that secretly monitors or records a user's activity.   - Adware:     - Adware is a type of malware that displays unwanted advertisements. The types of malware include viruses, worms, spyware, and adware, each with its own unique characteristics and purposes. Draft Learner can click on each type of malware to learn more. Content Characteristics and Consequences • Visual description: A table summarizing the characteristics and consequences of each type of malware. • Characteristics and Consequences:   - Virus:     - Characteristics: Replicates itself, attaches to other programs or files.     - Consequences: Can cause system crashes, data loss, or identity theft.   - Worm:     - Characteristics: Spreads from computer to computer without human intervention, can cause system crashes or data loss.     - Consequences: Can cause system crashes, data loss, or identity theft.   - Spyware:     - Characteristics: Secretly monitors or records user activity, can cause system crashes or data loss.     - Consequences: Can lead to identity theft, financial loss, or compromised online security. Understanding the characteristics and consequences of each type of malware is crucial in protecting your computer and personal data. Draft Learner can review the table to reinforce their knowledge. Content Real-World Examples • Visual description: A series of real-world examples illustrating the impact of malware on individuals and organizations. • Real-World Examples:   - Example 1: A virus infected a company's computer system, causing a data loss of $1 million.   - Example 2: A worm spread through a university's network, causing a system crash and resulting in a loss of $500,000. Malware can have devastating consequences, including financial loss, data loss, and compromised online security. It is essential to be aware of the risks and take proactive measures to protect yourself and your organization. Draft Learner can review the examples to understand the impact of malware. MODULE 5: Social Engineering

SECTION TOPICS VISUAL INSTRUCTIONS/DEVELOPER NOTES ON-SCREEN TEXT AUDIO NARRATION STATUS ACTIONS REQUIRED Intro Definition of Social Engineering • Visual description of a person being tricked by a scammer • Layout details with a background image of a busy office • Social engineering is a type of cyber attack that tricks people into revealing sensitive information or performing certain actions • It can be carried out through various means, including email, phone, or in-person interactions Social engineering is a type of cyber attack that tricks people into revealing sensitive information or performing certain actions. It can be carried out through various means, including email, phone, or in-person interactions. The goal of social engineering is to gain the trust of the victim and manipulate them into doing something that they wouldn't normally do. This can be a powerful tool for hackers, as it allows them to gain access to sensitive information or systems without having to use any technical skills. Draft Create a scenario where the learner is presented with a social engineering attack and must decide how to respond Content Types of Social Engineering Attacks • Visual description of a person being targeted by a phishing email • Types of social engineering attacks include phishing, pretexting, baiting, tailgating, and impersonation • Phishing is when an attacker sends a fake email or message that appears to be from a legitimate source, asking the victim to reveal sensitive information • Pretexting is when an attacker creates a false scenario or story to gain the trust of the victim and get them to reveal sensitive information In this section, we will discuss the different types of social engineering attacks. Phishing is a common type of attack where an attacker sends a fake email or message that appears to be from a legitimate source, asking the victim to reveal sensitive information. Pretexting is another type of attack where an attacker creates a false scenario or story to gain the trust of the victim and get them to reveal sensitive information. Draft Create a case study of a phishing attack and have the learner identify the warning signs Content Warning Signs of Social Engineering Attacks • Visual description of a person being suspicious of a phone call • Warning signs of social engineering attacks include suspicious phone calls or emails, requests for sensitive information, and unsolicited offers or requests • If you receive a call or email that seems suspicious, it's best to err on the side of caution and not reveal any sensitive information In this section, we will discuss the warning signs of social engineering attacks. If you receive a call or email that seems suspicious, it's best to err on the side of caution and not reveal any sensitive information. Draft Create a scenario where the learner is presented with a suspicious phone call or email and must decide how to respond Interaction Social Engineering Attack Simulation • Visual description of a person being targeted by a social engineering attack • Learner must identify the warning signs of the attack and decide how to respond In this section, we will simulate a social engineering attack and have the learner identify the warning signs and decide how to respond. The learner will be presented with a scenario where they are being targeted by an attacker and must use their knowledge of social engineering to make a decision. Draft Create a branching scenario where the learner's decisions affect the outcome Review Recap of Social Engineering • Visual description of a person reviewing a presentation • Recap of key points, including types of social engineering attacks and warning signs In this section, we will recap the key points of social engineering, including the types of attacks and the warning signs. The learner will have the opportunity to review the material and ask questions. SECTION TOPICS VISUAL INSTRUCTIONS/DEVELOPER NOTES ON-SCREEN TEXT AUDIO NARRATION STATUS ACTIONS REQUIRED Intro Importance of Cyber Security Best Practices • Visualize a graph showing the increase in cyber attacks over the years • Use a simple layout with a few icons • Cyber security best practices are essential to protect against cyber threats • Regular updates and password management are crucial to prevent cyber attacks The increasing number of cyber attacks demands a robust cyber security strategy, which includes implementing best practices. These practices help protect against various types of cyber threats and ensure the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of data. Regular updates and password management are crucial to prevent cyber attacks. By following cyber security best practices, organizations can reduce the risk of cyber attacks and protect their reputation. Draft Review content for accuracy and update visuals as necessary Content Password Management • Use an infographic to illustrate the importance of strong passwords • Include a few examples of weak and strong passwords • Use unique and complex passwords for each account • Avoid using the same password for multiple accounts • Change passwords regularly Password management is a critical aspect of cyber security. Using strong, unique, and complex passwords for each account can help prevent unauthorized access. Avoid using the same password for multiple accounts, and change passwords regularly to minimize the risk of cyber attacks. Draft Add more examples of weak and strong passwords to illustrate the concept Content Firewalls • Use an animation to demonstrate how firewalls work • Include a diagram showing the different types of firewalls • Firewalls act as a barrier between the internal and external networks • They prevent unauthorized access to the network and protect against malware and viruses Firewalls are a crucial component of cyber security. They act as a barrier between the internal and external networks, preventing unauthorized access and protecting against malware and viruses. There are different types of firewalls, including hardware and software firewalls, network-based firewalls, and host-based firewalls. Install and regularly update antivirus software, and run regular virus scans to detect and remove malware. This helps prevent cyber attacks and ensures the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of data.
